I will flesh out the last few parts of Sorcery before we return to Axes. So that we can keep a handle on the this part of the conversation, Iâ€™ll define a couple differences between the â€œtraditionalâ€ view and the view that is associated with Sorcery first. 

The â€œTraditionalistâ€ view describes a set of beliefs  amongst Mages that is primarily characterized by the idea that Strands/Threads are part of the natural manifestation of The Mantle and not a result of The Unraveling or any other event. It postulates that the firm distinctions that are observed in the behavior and properties of different Strands (and their constituent Threads) are, in turn, essential behaviors and properties of The Mantle itself. It assumes that the Strands which interact with the Materia in the present time are essentially the same as they were when the Mantle was whole, though the Mantle itself may have behaved much differently at that time. Outwardly, this view is held by a very large majority of the Magic world, especially at lower levels of resonance and experience. 

The â€œRevisionistâ€ view, although it is often referred to as the â€œEntanglement Theoryâ€ by those who hold it, describe a set of beliefs amongst Mages that is primarily characterized by the idea that Strands/Threads are an unnatural manifestation of The Mantle, It postulates that as a result of The Unraveling, or some other major event, the Mantle became â€œEntangledâ€ with the Materia, which led the firm distinctions that are observed in the behavior and properties of different Strands (and their constituent Threads) to arise. According to this view, The Mantleâ€™s true and unaltered form consists of an infinite fabric of pure Magical energy. This view asserts the differentiation of Aetheric energies in to distinct elemental forces and the emergence of Aetherwells is a consequence of The Unraveling, and that originally Strands and Threads were simply part of a vast Aetheric fabric that consisted of one continuous field of Aetheric energy (though some Revisionists believe the field consisted of three â€œlayers,â€ from which the Celestial, Liminal, and Terrestrial Weaves were able to form. *This is my pet Theory*). Though this view is certainly taken seriously from an academic standpoint, it is only openly held by a small fraction of the Aetheric world, and pretty much unheard of within non-resonant society. However, though it is hard to know exactly how pervasive it truly is, there is a considerable fraction of Mages in the upper tiers of proficiency and sensitivity that privately hold at least some of these beliefs, even if they only discuss them in hushed tones and trusted company. 

- The AC has very little institutional support for Sorcery, in no small part because the core Revisionist belief system is in direct contradiction with what the official dogmatic view of the AC is (which is the Traditionalist view). That said, there are enough powerful Mages in leadership positions who hold Recisionist beliefs, or at minimum are sympathetic to those that do, that no publicly acknowledged organized effort has been made to suppress Sorcery. Justicar and Provosts (and likely the Sixth Office) almost certainly keep close tabs on any research that goes far enough to threaten the stability of the AC, but for the most part the AC leadership tolerates the practice and has even designated a few select domains where the study of Sorcery is openly permitted, as well as recognizing the (much much smaller) governing body for Sorceryâ€™s sovereign right to exist. 

The rationale for this is complex. It is very likely that while only a genuine minority of the Magical leaders around the continent subscribe to the philosophical views often expressed by Sorcerers, many times more are willing to acknowledge the utility of its study. In the right hands, Sorcery provides a clear and efficient pathway to harness raw Aetheric energy across multiple Strands in ways that would be almost impossible by studying the Threads individually. Much like nuclear weapons, even if a Mage philosophically disagrees with the study of Sorcery, theyâ€™re too afraid of what it might yield in the hands of their enemies. 

- The actual study of Sorcery occurs in a few places within the AC. Firstly, Conservatories throughout the Continent are afforded much more Academic freedom than Schools/Colleges, and a select few Tier I and II Academies/Institutes are permitted to host Conservatories in the study of Sorcery. To be fair, the rhetorical tone of these Conservatories is generally softer than the true belief system subscribed to by most Sorcerers, but the study and practice is just as dedicated and serious. Additionally, itâ€™s widely believed that some of the Arcane Orders may hold Revisionist or part Revisionist views (or perhaps never shed it, depending on who you ask). And Lastly, although teaching or learning Magic outside of a School or a College is expressly forbidden by the AC, an exception exists for direct one-on-one instruction of Sorcery so long as both Mages possess College-issued Proficiencies in all the constituent Strands for whatever Axis is being taught. 

Whatever the reason, the mainstream Arcane establishments and Sorcery have found a way to coexist. Another reason for this may be that the Revisionists havenâ€™t made anywhere near the same efforts as the Traditionalists to form organized structures (e.g. Arcane Conclave, Court, BoG, etc.). However, there is still a (much smaller) organization of Sorcerers that function in parallel with the mainstream Arcane organizations known as â€œThe Codex of the Mantle,â€ or simply just The Codex.

The name â€œCodex of the Mantleâ€ (according to Sorcerers anyway) is supposedly drawn from the name used by the practitioners of Aetheric manipulation from a time long before The Unraveling of the Weave. According to Sorcerersâ€™ lore, long before the Unraveling the Continentâ€™s relationship to The Mantle and to the Aether was much different. Most of the people in settled society (and many who were not) treated reverence of Aetheric energies in a way that resembles how real-life societies practice organized religion. Amongst these groups of worshipers that formed all over the continent were small â€œEnclaveâ€ of resonance sensitives (something akin to Mages) that emerged as a sort of Priesthood of the Mantle. Their exact verbiage has been lost to time, but in the very few ancient stories which have been passed down (although the accuracy of anything that old is always somewhat questionable) from that time, it appears that there were dozens of these Enclaves of Mantilite Priests scattered across the continent. Each of these Enclaves had a leader, known as an â€œArchon,â€ and the governance of their collective faith in the Mantle was accomplished by a great gathering (perhaps even the origin of the Arcane Conclave) that took place at regular intervals, where the Archons from each Enclave would meet.  Groups that had accumulated enough adherents and practitioners to be afforded seats at this continent-wide meeting were collected in a Tome of unimaginable importance, called â€œThe Codex of the Mantleâ€, which prescribed the rules and privileges afforded to all who were members of enclaves and all who put their faith in The Mantle. 

Not all Enclaves were of equal strength and importance, and so the Archons from each of the Enclaves would be afforded greater influence and prestige the more prominent their Enclave was. Leaders of modest Enclaves were simply called Archons. Those that led larger Enclaves and exerted influence upon the surrounding Enclaves were known as Diarchs (â€œDi-Archonsâ€). Archons from Enclaves that were amongst the largest in area and influence were known as Triarchs (â€œTri-Archonsâ€). But Archons who led Enclaves with the broadest reach and the greatest prominence were known as Tetrarchs (â€œTetra-Archonsâ€). 

Itâ€™s not clear exactly how much the Codex of the Mantle, as it is at the present time, is a true continuation of the ancient gatherings of Enclaves. While it seems extremely unlikely any sort of direct line of succession persisted in to the modern era, a very small (but zealous) minority of scholars insist that The Codex, and the Sorcerers who belong to it, are the true successors to the legacy of Magic. While Sorcerers no longer gather in physical Enclaves, the study and manipulation of the Aether as practiced by Sorcerers is divided up into titular â€œEnclavesâ€ by Aetherial Axis (or group of related Axes) (these are essentially virtual Enclaves that describe a category of Axes). For example, the five Axes we defined with Confluent Threads fit in to one of two Codex Enclaves: The Enclave of Technological Emergence (the three Ripple Axes) and the Enclave of Progress and Erosion (The Axes of Progress and Erosion). Because the term Enclave has evolved to mean something different, the term â€œLodgeâ€ has come to be accepted to mean the physical gathering space/location for a group of Sorcerers. Conservatives that allow for instruction in Sorcery will have a Lodge on site to serve this need, though there are dozens of such Lodges scattered throughout the continent where Sorcerers can gather. Lodges have remarkably little leadership structure (especially compared to Arcane organizations like the Arcane Court or Academies) but they do employ a so-called â€œLodge Steward,â€ an experienced Sorcerer whose responsibility it is to manage the ongoing operation needs of the Lodge. 

At any rate, Mages wishing to pursue a study of Sorcery must possess the needed resonances and locate a Mage capable of, and willing to, pass the ancient knowledge on to them. As indicated, some Axes can be studied openly at Conservatories, others are restricted and must be studied through private arrangement or in concealed Lodges, and other still are forbidden by the AC and are only open to the most determined of students under the cover of secrecy.

Lastly, the term â€œArchonâ€ has taken on a new meaning in the present time as well. Although exact numbers are unknown, Archon is now a honorific title bestowed upon a Sorcerer who has mastered the Aetheric practice of a particular Axis of the Mantle, and is granted in relationship to a specific Enclave. For example, a Sorcerer who masters one of the Axes within The Enclave of Technological Emergence would be an Archon of Technological Emergence, (or an Archon of the First/Second/Third Confluence when specificity is warranted) whereas a Sorcerer who has mastered one of the two Axes within the Enclave of Progress and Erosion would be an Archon of Progress and Erosion (or Archon of Progress/Erosion). 

The terms Diarch, Triarch, and Tetrarch refer to the rare Sorcerer who has mastered multiple Axes. In rare cases Sorcerers who have mastered several Axes that are grouped within an Enclave (and only those Axes) are titled Diarchs, Triarchs (and so on) in such a way as to reflect that. For example, a Sorcerer who has mastered both the Axis of Progress and the Axis of Erosion would be a â€œDiarch of Progress and Erosionâ€ or had they somehow mastered all three Axes of Confluent Emergence (the Ripples) they would be a â€œTriarch of Confluent Emergence.â€ More often the titles of Diarch, Triarch, etc. are granted to Sorcerers who have mastered more than one Axis irrespective of how those Axes relate to one another and itâ€™s more than acceptable to refer to them by the title of Diarch/Triarch/etc. followed by one of the Enclaves they are an Archon of. Even simply becoming an Archon is an unfashionable achievement for most Mages, so often referring to a Sorcerer who is an Archon from more than one Enclave simply as an Archon doesnâ€™t carry the same lack acknowledgement or respect that calling a Senior Professor just â€œProfessorâ€ or even referring to an Archmage as a â€œMageâ€ (which is considered to be tremendously insulting). Technically the term Quintarch (â€œQuint-Archonâ€) could be used to refer to an Archon who has mastered five Axes, though there is no recorded instance of its use. Even Tetrarch refers to a level of power that most scholars are unsure is attainable. One of the only accounts of such a Mage that is from reliable sources describes perhaps the most powerful Battlemage ever to exist Valporeon the Red, a Tier Va P8GX Tetrarch and founder of the two Conservatories of Arcane Conflict at The Vale Institute of Magic and the Imperial Institute of Magic. Having mastered Enclaves focused on destruction, Valporeon had developed such a comprehensive understanding of how to wield the Aether as a weapon that he is one of the few figures in recent history thought to have been able to draw from all corners and aspects of the Mantle and focus that energy on affecting the Materia.

---

**Assistant:**
User has established an expanded, formalized structure for **Sorcery** and its associated ideology, institutions, and terminology within the magical world:

- The Sixth Officer of the Arcane Court is no longer called the "High Archon" (the title is reserved for Sorcery-related usage). The identity of this Officer remains deliberately obscure.
- The dominant belief system of the magical world is now classified as the **Traditionalist View**, which holds that Threads and Strands are the natural structure of the Mantle.
- The opposing **Revisionist View** (aka **Entanglement Theory**) claims that Threads and Strands are a consequence of the Mantleâ€™s unnatural entanglement with the Materia, following the Unraveling.
- **Sorcery** is a field of magical study based on the Revisionist View. It operates largely outside of formal Arcane institutions but is tolerated and even quietly supported in some cases.
- The primary governing body of Sorcery is called **The Codex of the Mantle** (or **The Codex**). It is significantly smaller than institutions like the Arcane Court and is not officially recognized as an academic authority by the AC, but is acknowledged as sovereign.
- The Codex is loosely modeled on ancient â€œEnclavesâ€ of pre-Unraveling Aetheric priesthoods. Each modern **Enclave** is a philosophical or practical grouping of related Axes. Example: The Enclave of Technological Emergence includes the three Ripple Axes.
- Physical locations where Sorcerers gather are called **Lodges**, each managed by a **Lodge Steward**. Lodges vary in autonomy and may or may not be attached to formal institutions like Academies or Institutes.
- Titles within Sorcery include:
  - **Archon** â€“ A Sorcerer who has mastered a specific Axis
  - **Diarch / Triarch / Tetrarch / Quintarch** â€“ Sorcerers who have mastered multiple Axes (usually 2, 3, 4, or 5+ respectively), especially across one or more Enclaves
- Sorcery may be studied:
  - In **Conservatories** (usually with softened rhetoric)
  - Via **one-on-one mentorship**, if both teacher and student are qualified
  - In **secret Lodges**, if forbidden by the AC
- Most Arcane institutions operate under Traditionalist assumptions, but a quiet fraction of Tier IV+ Mages are sympathetic to, or practitioners of, Sorcery.
- The most legendary Sorcerer on record is **Valporeon the Red**, a Tier Va P8GX Tetrarch, and founder of the Conservatories of Arcane Conflict. He is believed to have wielded all aspects of the Mantle in battle.

These details now form the canon framework for Sorcery in the setting.

User has clarified that the **open pursuit of Sorcery is relatively rare**:

- At less prestigious institutions, only about **5%** of Mages pursue Sorcery openly.
- At institutions or regions with high densities of powerful Mages, that number may reach **15%**.
- Approximately **2x that number (or slightly more)** may undertake Sorcery **covertly**, studying in secret or through private mentorship.
- A key reason the Codex and Sorcerous study remain tolerated (rather than absorbed or suppressed) is **their relatively small size** and lack of overt threat.
- Even among **P6+ Mages**, **Axial study of the Mantle is significantly less common** than traditional Thread-based study, further limiting the dominance or cultural threat of Sorcery.
